Local News

Yesterday's Silver Price Continues to Plunge

Chinese Gold Continues to Leave the Country, Foreign Silver Continuously Imports

Gold Prices Soar, Silver Prices Plunge

The Whole Country is on the Verge of Bankruptcy, the Government Has No Solution

The price of silver has been gradually declining since January of this year. Today, the fall is even more severe. The whole country is shaken, saying that its devastation is greater than that of artillery fire. The Chinese authorities have been deliberating on ways to save the situation for some time, but no measures have been taken until recently, when the export ban of silver was implemented. But yesterday, the North China Daily News said that the result of the silver export ban is the opposite. When the ban was implemented, there were less than 3,000 gold bars in Shanghai. However, the total amount of miscellaneous gold from the mainland has greatly increased. The price of gold bars is close to 600 taels. There will be even more mainland gold bars and gold ornaments collected in Shanghai. There are also proposals to levy import silver tax to compensate in one or two ways, as said by the China Press. But a few days ago, the government firmly denied that there was such a proposal. What is the solution to saving the situation? This has to rely on the comprehensive planning of national economists and implement it as soon as possible. The situation has now become like a prairie fire. It is no longer possible to take a bystander attitude and let it take its course. The shocking news of yesterday is recorded as follows

Gold Prices Continue to Soar: At the Gold Exchange yesterday morning, the opening price was 577 taels, the highest was 598 and a half taels, and the afternoon closing price was 587 taels and 8 qian. The price of gold ornaments at Datong Silver Shop was 83 yuan.

Foreign Silver Still Being Imported: Since the National Government ordered the ban on foreign silver imports, the United Kingdom and the United States have still shipped large silver bars. The Japanese mail ship Hakusan Maru has arrived in Shanghai and loaded 216 large silver bars shipped from London, which have been unloaded. It is reported that a U.S. liner will arrive in Shanghai next Monday with a large batch of U.S. silver bars. It is still unknown whether they will be unloaded in Shanghai.

Investigation of Chinese Gold Being Transported to the United States: Yesterday, according to a reliable investigation in financial circles, from January to the end of March this year, a total of 275,156 cash bars were transported from China to New York in three months, accounting for 39,308 gold cakes (each 10 taels as one bar, every 7 bars become one cake) worth 5,687,410 US dollars, with an average of 42 yuan, equivalent to 13,541,450 taels of Shanghai silver. Already shocking enough, but the exports in April were even more alarming. During the entire month, there were 184,793 bars, accounting for 26,399 gold cakes worth 3,711,344 US dollars, with an average of 40 yuan, equivalent to 9,278,360 taels of Shanghai silver, actually exceeding the average number of exports in the above three months by more than one time. In May, because the government banned exports, they did not dare to openly report to customs and direct shipping. Because there are no detailed statistics for the exact number, there are still more than 100,000 bars of amounts exported by private transport, other goods, false reports, or smuggling that can be observed in the trade. In addition, in recent years, the old gold ornaments collected by silversmiths have been melted into cakes, which is uncountable.

Cotton Cloth Industry Appeals: The Shanghai Special City Cotton Cloth Association submitted a document to the Shanghai Merchants Federation saying: "Respectfully, according to reports from our members, they have sent representatives to the association, claiming that the price of silver continues to fall, causing a drastic contraction. Not only is there no turnaround, but new prices are also emerging repeatedly. The government has stated that it will provide relief, but so far there are no specific measures. If this continues, all of us in the industry, as well as import and export merchants, will be in a desperate situation. Please refer to the Shanghai Merchants Federation to quickly unite relevant groups and appeal to the government to provide relief to alleviate our suffering." After checking, since the price of gold is expensive and the price of silver is cheap, our industry has been the first to bear the brunt, and other industries have also been greatly affected, causing Shanghai's finances to become unstable. Suspensions and bankruptcies occur from time to time. The crisis is hidden, and the dangers are all around. The seriousness of the situation is unbearable. If no remedies are taken quickly, it will inevitably lead to economic bankruptcy. This city is the center of commerce and the hub of finance. A single hair affects the whole body, and the disaster will spread to the whole country. Considering this, we are deeply worried. We believe that the Shanghai Merchants Federation leads the merchants and has always been committed to protecting the welfare of merchants and alleviating their suffering. For this precarious situation, we should have plans to respond and report the situation. We hope that you will convene an emergency meeting and invite representatives from the chambers of commerce of various countries to attend the meeting to discuss solutions. On the one hand, we will unite relevant groups and appeal to the government for relief to save the crisis and alleviate the suffering of merchants. With utmost urgency, we await your command." To the Shanghai Merchants Federation.

The Ninth District Party Department Telegraphs: The Ninth District Party Department of this city believes that the gold market has recently undergone a drastic change, with the highest price of more than 577 taels, which has created a new record that has never been seen before. People are in danger and cannot live in peace. The cause of this is directly due to the contradiction between the exchange rate and extreme imperialism. The exchange rate is indirectly affected by the speculative market. The only solution at present is for the Ministry of Industry and Commerce to order the gold market to stop operations immediately in accordance with Article 41 of the Exchange Law because it endangers the public interest and disturbs public security. Then, find other ways to remedy the situation. As for the people, the united use of domestic products is one way to stop the loss of foreign exchange and save the national economy. Therefore, the City Executive Committee was specifically presented with a request to send a telegram to the central government to inform the National Government for verification so as to stabilize social morale and consolidate the rear order. The original presentation was thousands of words long, which is omitted here.

Japan Should be Held Responsible: The Wenhui Daily reported that the contraction of the foreign exchange market has created a strange situation that has never happened before. This morning (the 4th), the British exchange rate was reduced to one shilling, five pence, and two qian. The price of gold rose to 596 taels. Even at 2:30 in the afternoon, the price was still 586 taels and 5 qian. The market is unusually chaotic. There is no way to predict the future trend. Rumors are rife. Only time will tell how it ends up. According to the Japanese Mainichi Shimbun, Japan's gold ban is responsible for a large part of the reason why the price of silver has fallen so badly this year. Everyone knows that the Indian government's sale of silver and the large amount of silver flowing into China and hoarding in Shanghai are the main reasons for the fall in the price of silver. I don't know that Japan has a great relationship. In order to prevent the outflow of cash after the Japanese government lifted the ban, it asked various foreign exchange banks to provide spiritual assistance. Therefore, banks such as Mitsui and Mitsubishi absorbed cash in Shanghai after lifting the ban and transported it to the United States. According to the US Department of Commerce and the San Francisco Federation Reserve Bank, the amount of cash transferred to the United States in the past four months is as follows:

January: From Japan: ¥721,485. From China: ¥99,253

February: From Japan: ¥40,906,014. From China: ¥1,809,703

March: From Japan: ¥38,315,706. From China: ¥3,711,344

April: From Japan: ¥16,425.

(Translator's note: This table may contain omissions. According to statistics, the gold bars transferred to the United States from Shanghai in January to April alone were worth US$9,398,754.)

Looking at the above table, the cash transported to the United States from China has increased sharply since March, and the gold bars transported to Japan in April are also worth ¥2 million. This is why the Nanjing government had to ban the export of gold. The balance of gold and silver reserves in the Shanghai market has been lost, resulting in a sharp drop in the price of silver. As a result, the London and New York silver markets were affected, and the repercussions were enough to affect the Shanghai market. Therefore, the export of cash in the Shanghai market has actually been doubly affected, and the cause of this is the Japanese government. However, after the sharp drop in the price of silver, Sino-Japanese trade has been at a disadvantage, especially the export of Japanese cotton yarn to China. As a result, Japanese financiers and large merchants of yarn, cloth, sugar, and flour have blamed their government for lifting the ban too early and for the errors in the policies adopted after lifting the ban.

Quickly Implement Silver Tax Collection: The China Press editorial on the 4th said that the price of the British pound has risen to 19 yuan, and the price of silver has plummeted. The trend of the downward trend is increasing every moment. What will be the final result? China's bankruptcy is imminent, and it is useless to flatter the officials. If we do not find a way to stop the influx of low-priced silver like a raging tide in this major commercial port, China will be in ruin. Is there a political relationship between the foreign financiers' cruel actions and only one way to resist foreign activities? This matter must be dealt with with courage. We believe that even if the government levies silver taxes at this time, it can still make up for the loss and allow struggling merchants and bankers to benefit slightly. Today, it is not only these two types of people who are in danger of bankruptcy. The whole country is in this danger. What will be the result? It's unthinkable. Alas, China is now able to fight bravely on the battlefield. Why is it so cowardly and indecisive behind the battle? France's Poincaré once said that only courage and creativity can save a country's bankruptcy. Today, if China wants to save the situation, it must immediately implement resolute plans. The country's misfortunes can produce such great people? Now is the time.

The Arsenal Still Worked as Usual Yesterday

The Loss in the Bullet Loading Room the Day Before Yesterday was Very Small

Guo Chengen, director of the Shanghai Arsenal, told the National News Agency reporter yesterday that at 8:10 a.m. on Tuesday morning, an explosion suddenly occurred when workers gathered in the bullet loading room. The cause of the explosion is currently being investigated by experts, but there is absolutely no sabotage by villains. Because all the workers used have been serving for a long time and are extremely reliable, and the defense is strict and no strangers can break in. The material loss in this explosion was very small, worth less than 6,000 yuan. Because the loading of medicine is all done manually and not by machines, so is the material loss is not large. Unfortunately, six people died on the spot and twenty-five were injured, several of whom were seriously injured. The bullet loading room is far away from the manufacturing factory, so the factory has not been affected at all. It is still working as usual without any interruption.

The Ministry of Navy Plans

Additional Purchase of New Survey Vessels

Drawing from the Boxer Indemnity Fund for Purchase

Dedicated to Surveying, Not to Be Used for Other Purposes

The Hydrographic Office directly under the Naval Department, located at Fenglin Bridge in this city, currently lacks sufficient survey vessels to allocate for its work. In order to plan for the development of surveying tasks, it is proposed to draw from the British Boxer Indemnity Fund to purchase several new survey vessels to facilitate operations. A draft proposal for drawing funds has been submitted to the Naval Department for review by the National Government. The original text of the proposal is excerpted as follows: (1) Purchase two new survey vessels fully equipped with all kinds of new surveying instruments; (2) These two vessels should be built in British Hong Kong, ready for use upon arrival; (3) The contract should specify that these two vessels are exclusively for surveying purposes and not for other equipment; (4) Allocate the remaining funds to a trusted organization designated by both parties, specifically for the annual repair and consumption of the two new vessels. Funds should not be used for any other purposes unrelated to surveying. The department believes that surveying rivers and seas benefits domestic and foreign merchants, ensuring the safety of all voyages, which is a matter of international public interest. Drawing from the Boxer Indemnity Fund will surely gain British sympathy. Instructions have already been given to the office to comprehensively plan and draft a proposed budget for submission to the department for approval.

Baoshan Meeting on Preventing Rice Stem Borers

Baoshan County Magistrate Qiu Mingjiu convened a meeting at 2:00 PM yesterday in the west hall of the county government to discuss measures to prevent pests. Present were Bei Jietai, Huang Cengmu, Ji Zhonghe, Cai Youchang, Xue Yingpu, Wen Gui (representing Chen Zaofeng), Ma Mengyuan (representative of the Traffic Department), Sun Qixian, Shen Jing, Qiu Mingjiu, Wang Tongchuan, and Ge Zuwang (County Party Committee). County Magistrate Qiu chaired the meeting and reported on the following: (1) Received a letter from the Agricultural College of the Labor University stating that rice seedlings in the college's field area have recently been found to be infested with rice stem borers, enclosing promotional materials for distribution to farmers for unified capture and burning, etc. The letter has been transmitted to all districts and farms. (1) Found in the takeover documents an order from the Department of Agriculture and Mining informing all counties that expenses for controlling rice stem borers are approved as legitimate expenditures. Discussion items: (1) Should branch associations for the prevention of rice stem borers be established in each district? Resolved: Branch associations have already been established in each district. They should intensify their work and earnestly publicize. If more branch associations can be organized, efforts should be made to organize them. (1) Publicity methods: Resolved: a. In addition to the promotional materials issued by the county government, each district chief should convene the township heads under their jurisdiction to provide practical guidance to the people on preventing rice stem borers. b. Starting next Tuesday (June 10), the county magistrate will invite the director of the farm to personally go to each district to convene the township heads and deputies for talks and guidance on preventing rice stem borers. The departure dates are as follows: June 10 afternoon to the first district, June 11 morning to the fifth district, June 12 morning to the fourth district, June 13 morning to the second district, June 14 morning to the third district. (1) Methods for purchasing rice stem borer eggs: Resolved: Temporarily set the price at three copper coins per two taels of rice stem borer eggs. Each district should submit them to the county government weekly for payment. (1) Methods for purchasing rice stem borer moths: Resolved: Temporarily set the price at six copper coins per two taels of rice stem borer moths. Each district should submit them to the county government weekly for payment.

Approximate Amount of Zhejiang Tea Transported to Shanghai

7,162 Boxes Have Arrived

The Shanghai-Hangzhou Railway is transporting boxed tea produced in Jin, Qu, Yan, and other places in Zhejiang Province to Shanghai for sale overseas. Huitong and Maoshuntai Transfer Companies have contracted with the railway bureau to transport the tea. Shipping began in late last month, and the tea has been continuously loaded at the Gate Station and transported to Shanghai. As of yesterday, the approximate amount that had arrived in Shanghai was 7,162 boxes. It is reported that there are still over 5,000 boxes of tea loaded onto barges at Shangjiang waiting to be transported to the Gate Station, all of which need to be loaded onto trains. Therefore, freight trains have been running daily from the station to Shanghai, and it is estimated that the total number of boxes of tea will be around 200,000 by the end of the season.

Decline in Upriver Yangtze Shipping

River Steamers Change to Coastal Routes

British Companies Reduce Ships, Starting This Month, the Yangtze Upriver Business Has Sharply Declined, With No Goods for Import or Export. One of the Hunan-bound steamers of the Nissin Company has been suspended. British companies operating on the Yuezhou, Shashi, Xiangtan, and Changsha routes have also suspended their regular steamers due to lack of cargo and have temporarily dispatched several tugboats to load scattered goods in Hunan and Hubei. The Taikoo Company decided yesterday to temporarily suspend the Chongqing steamer, which was originally running the Shanghai-Hankou route, and switch it to the Beiyang route because the Yangtze River was short of cargo. It is unusual for a Yangtze River steamer to be transferred to a coastal route.

Japanese Warships Head to Hunan. The First Japanese Overseas Expeditionary Force has dispatched six warships, including the Sumida and Ataka, to Yuezhou and further to Changsha. Furthermore, Commander Minai of the fleet personally led the shallow-draft warships Atami and Futami, along with a naval group, to continue to Changsha.

River Pilots Return to Work. Foreign steamships operating on the Yichang-Chongqing route were opposed to the increase in salary for river pilots. After the Japanese and American ships agreed to increase salaries, British steamships such as Taikoo and Jardine Matheson resolutely refused to increase them, and the foreign companies hired their own drivers. This matter has been reported in this newspaper. It is reported that the situation has been mediated by various parties, and the British companies have also realized the difficulty of operating on the Sichuan River and have accepted the demands of the river pilots, agreeing to appropriately increase their salaries. Starting this month, all Chinese river pilots on foreign steamships operating upriver have returned to work.

County Finance Bureau Urges Payment of Old Debts

Wang Li, Director of the Shanghai County Finance Bureau, found that the amount of old rice tax and other tax revenues owed in the county was enormous. During this time of military affairs, the provincial government is urgently urging the remittance of funds, so it is imperative to organize the collection. Therefore, he summoned the heads of the six districts under the county at 2:00 PM yesterday to discuss the matter, ordering that the old rice tax owed from the 17th and 18th years of the Republic be paid in full within five mao (five days per mao). Those who are lazy or deliberately resist will be reported for arrest. Furthermore, Director Wang believes that there is still over 10,000 yuan of old rice tax owed from the 16th year of the Republic when the city and county were not divided. The original collectors should be held responsible for urging payment. Therefore, he ordered that the collectors who have been assigned to the city should be summoned to the bureau today to discuss the matter, limiting the time for urging payment in order to emphasize national taxation.

End of Labor Conscription for Road Construction

The Shanghai County Construction Bureau received instructions from the Jiangsu Construction Department stating that labor conscription for road construction in various counties should be temporarily suspended due to the current busy farming season. The labor conscription and road construction promotion associations, labor conscription and road construction offices, and labor conscription assistants set up for labor conscription and road construction should be abolished. Furthermore, the number of personnel used by the highway offices attached to various bureaus is still considerable and should be effectively reduced to comply with the principle of austerity policy. The temporary technicians set up by various counties for labor conscription and road construction are similar in nature to labor conscription assistants and should also be abolished at the same time. If counties need to carry out supplementary surveying, supervision, and construction of bridges and culverts, they should be allocated separately according to the needs of the work and reported for verification. Director Wu is now complying with the order and reporting the progress of labor conscription and road construction to the Construction Department for approval.

Shipping Merchants in Shanghai

Continued Report on Opposition to Foreign Steamships Stopping at Anqing

Requesting the Anhui Provincial Government to Fundamentally Cancel This Case

The Anhui authorities' approval for foreign steamships to dock at Anqing and establish public docks to collect taxes has been opposed by shipping merchants in Shanghai. The Ministry of Foreign Affairs has replied to the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company, agreeing to consult with the Anhui Provincial Government to temporarily suspend this case, not wanting to benefit some at the expense of others. After the reply arrived in Shanghai, shipping merchants still considered it unsatisfactory because temporary suspension is not a fundamental cancellation. Li Fang, who proposed the establishment of docks, stated in his original report that "when I was in Anqing, various provincial government agencies believed that foreign ships coming and going to that place did not have wharves and did not anchor to pick up and drop off passengers, which was very dangerous. They instructed me to negotiate with the three foreign steamship companies to request that they dock at public wharves in the future." This statement completely ignores the facts. Steamships of Taikoo, Nissin, and Jardine Matheson have always stopped at Anqing without exception, and passengers and cargo have always been transported by private boats. Only the China Merchants and Sanbei steamships have been docking at the Anqing docks, with seventeen steamships. After the situation was stabilized, at least two steamships of Ning, Shao, Zhao, and Xing came and went every day. Even now, the China Merchants Steam Navigation Company's steamships are running daily. Yesterday, the shipping merchants decided on two measures: (1) First, order the Anqing branches to vigorously organize the docking of Chinese steamships at the docks to make it very convenient for passengers to embark and disembark, to prevent foreigners from making excuses. (2) The shipping merchants will submit a second report to the Ministry of Communications, requesting the Ministry of Foreign Affairs to consult with the Anhui Provincial Government to fundamentally cancel this case to comply with the government's intention to reclaim navigation rights.

Commercial Ship Driving Association Requests

Each Steamship to Add Third Mates and Apprentices

The Shipping Association yesterday sent a letter to various steamship companies stating that it had previously received a letter from the China Merchant Ship Drivers Association stating that recently, whenever shipping companies in various places purchased ships or replaced foreign crew members, they wanted to hire Chinese, but Chinese often lamented the lack of talent. The reason is that although Chinese have emerged later, there is no shortage of people, but there are too few opportunities for practical apprenticeship, and there is a lack of experience, so it is often inconvenient to entrust them with important tasks. If this is not changed urgently, it is feared that after ten years, there will still be a shortage of Chinese navigators. Therefore, the association has repeatedly convened meetings and unanimously decided on two proposals: one is to request the government to designate steamship companies in various places to add third mates and apprentices, and the other is to discuss whether your association can automatically add third mates and apprentices. The general outline of the resolution at that time was that all ships navigating along the coast, regardless of size, must add two to four apprentices. Those with a gross tonnage of more than 2,000 tons or a sea voyage of more than five days should add one third mate. How to treat these crew members should be considered by your association to provide the best method so that both the capital side and the crew members can benefit. The association believes that only in this way can the navigators who emerge later have sufficient opportunities for practical experience, so that in the near future, we can avoid the criticism of borrowing talents from foreign countries. The association believes that our country is in a situation where various imperialist forces are invading, and only by uniting the whole country and cooperating in all aspects can we compete for survival. Your association is wise and understands, and I dare to offer the above suggestions for your consideration. I hope you will reply as soon as possible, etc. This was submitted to the 6th Executive Supervisory Committee meeting on May 31 for discussion. It was unanimously decided that in recent years, Chinese shipping has been affected by various factors and has reached its extreme point. It is difficult to maintain if expenses are increased again, and training maritime talents cannot be delayed. Each company has to consider the situation and try to recruit as much as possible for training and to protect navigation rights. The association will send letters to each member for consideration and reply to the association, etc. The case is recorded and presented for your reference and consideration.

Yesterday

Second General Meeting of the Chinese Medicine Association

Yesterday was the second general meeting of the Shanghai Special City Chinese Medicine Association. It was held at the Ningbo Fellow Association. More than 300 members and 60 guests attended. Xie Liheng, Ding Zhongying (represented by Guo Boliang), and Cai Jiping were elected as the presidium. Chen Yaotang was the master of ceremonies, and Chen Cunren and Cheng Diren were the recorders. The association then convened national medical groups to promote the National Medical Association. This is the most obvious external work of the association. (2) In order to cultivate talents, the association has taken over the Chinese Medical College for a year and has made considerable achievements. This is the most practical internal work of the association. In addition, all association affairs are detailed in the association publication, etc. Then, Yu Hongsun of the Finance Section reported on the income and expenditure briefly. (2) Expanding the organization of the association. A total of three articles were passed. (3) Asking various academic groups to subsidize the association's expenses. US Consulate to Rebuild New Building

Construction Cost 1.2 Million US Dollars

The US Consulate General in Shanghai has always been located on Huangpu Road. Due to its age and disrepair and insufficient office space, it has been approved by the US government to allocate a large sum of money to rebuild a new building on the original site. The estimated construction cost is 1.2 million US dollars. Construction is scheduled to begin on August 1 of this year and be completed in two years. The new building will be large in scale and fully equipped with the Consul General's office, consular offices, courts, dormitories, etc. After construction begins, the US Consulate will temporarily move to the corner of Jiangxi Road and Jiujiang Road.

This time, he was transferred from the US Embassy to the Ministry of Foreign Affairs, and the Ministry urgently telegraphed him to arrive as soon as possible, so he traveled to China as quickly as possible.

Major Fight in a Laundry Shop

Abdomen Burned by a Red-Hot Iron

Head Covered in Blood from a Door Bolt

A laundry shop opened by a certain Jia, a native of Shaoxing, at the entrance of Mingyangli, Manzhou Road, Zhabei, had a certain Gao Yunbo, a native of Tianjin, come to pick up a washed and ironed long gown the other day. Shop assistant He Chuer asked for the washing and ironing fee, and Gao said that he would deliver it to your boss another day, but He refused and scolded Gao for being a pig and putting on airs. Gao refused to accept this and got into a scuffle with He. At that time, another shop assistant, Chen Fuchun, was ironing clothes with a red-hot iron. Seeing Gao beat up his colleague, Chen immediately held the red-hot iron toward Gao in a threatening manner. Gao was afraid and pushed He violently, causing him to fall on Chen. Chen accidentally held the iron and touched his abdomen, causing the red-hot iron to burn his abdomen, scorching the skin and flesh. A piece of skin was burned off, and the blood and flesh were bright red, which was a terrible sight. At that time, a group of people outside the door named Qiu Songshan saw that their colleague was in trouble and immediately grabbed a door bolt and hit Gao's head hard. Gao was quick-eyed and agile and dodged the blow, but the stick hit He Chuer's forehead, creating a hole. Because he used his hand to block the stick, the iron hoop on the stick pierced his tiger's mouth, causing a wound about three-fen deep, and blood flowed all over his body. Then, the fourth assistant Chen Yuzhang stepped forward and threw Gao to the ground, and Qiu Songshan and Chen Yuzhang肆行 together, causing him to suffer several injuries from the wooden stick. Then, patrol officer Zhang Pinsan arrived and brought the group of people to the First Sub-Bureau of the Fourth District and transferred them to the Municipal Public Security Bureau for questioning.

A Quarrel Started from Urinating

Private Fight with Iron Bars and Files

Both Sides Injured and Arrested

Yesterday at noon, Qian Shuishui, a worker at the Yifeng Enamel Factory in Xieqiao, was scolded by Zhou Mingjin, a fellow worker from his hometown, for urinating against a wall outside the factory gate. This led to a verbal altercation, which escalated into a physical fight. Before long, each side gathered dozens of people, wielding iron bars and files to fight each other. As a result, both sides were badly injured, with heads broken and blood flowing. The Liyuan Road Police Station of the Second District Police Department learned of this and immediately dispatched an inspector with police officers to arrest those involved. They arrested nineteen people, including Qian Shuishui, Zhou Mingjin, Wang Zhenhai, Yu Bingda, Zhang Chaoguan, Gao Hongsheng, Peng Gencai, Qian Asi, Peng Xuesheng, Shen Jincai, Xu Shousheng, Feng Pusheng, Yang Yuru, Gao Cailin, Zhao Xiaoquan, Wang Fugeng, Xu Gencai, Wu Yonglian, and Yang Jindi, as well as the weapons used. They were escorted to the Second District Headquarters and, because the case involved injury, were immediately sent to the District Court for investigation.

Information Received by the Huining Fellow-Villagers Association Regarding Police Expenses in Jing County

The Huining Fellow-Villagers Association in Shanghai received a letter yesterday from Xiao Zhiquan, captain of the First Guerrilla Squad of the People's Self-Defense Corps in Jing County. It stated that on the night of May 29 at 2:00 AM, the squad's second squad leader reported hearing gunshots in the city. Upon receiving the report, the squad immediately directed all armed personnel to strengthen their posts and deploy defenses in the eastern part of the city. The captain personally led five members to investigate the truth. While passing through East Street, they encountered over seventy mutineering soldiers who opened fire. After a thirty-minute street battle, the squad, outnumbered, suffered the death of squad member Luo Jinbiao. For self-preservation, they had to retreat to the outside of the East Gate temporarily. They then led their troops back to attack, vigorously pursuing the mutineering soldiers, who fled toward the outside of the North Gate. The squad is now maintaining order in the city. In addition to pursuing and suppressing the mutineers, the captain fears that fellow villagers abroad may misunderstand the situation and become anxious. He is therefore reporting the facts and hopes the association will investigate.

Rock as

Fearless Sleeper

Feels Deeply Uneasy in America

Will Ask the American Consulate for Explanation

The lawsuit caused by the "Fearless Sleeper" film has been going on for nearly three months, and mediation is still underway. It is hoped that the case can be resolved amicably without going through legal channels, so the court has not set a date for continued hearings. It has been learned that Rock, the actor who played the lead role in the film, feels deeply uneasy after hearing about the matter in America. He has formally stated that when he played the role, he was purely motivated by interest and had no intention of insulting the Chinese. When the film was released in America, the Chinese community there did not point out any insults to the Chinese either. He did not expect that a misunderstanding would arise in Shanghai. He plans to write to the American Consulate in Shanghai for a detailed explanation to express his apology.

District Court Hearing

Shandong Bandit Chief

Hu Xiaozhong: Is He Really a Good Person?

Relying on Fellow Villagers from Linyi to Testify

Hu Xiaozhong, from Linyi, Shandong, was turned over to the Public Security Bureau last year in Shanghai's Fahua by Chen Qingtang, a fellow villager, who accused Hu of being a key member of the Shandong bandit Xie Liangcheng's gang. He allegedly led over 500 bandits on the night of August 25, 1928, to attack Chen's village, Nanquanzhuang, which is located ninety li from the city of Linyi, killing 143 men, women, and children, kidnapping 20 girls aged 15 to 20,陈的陈锡堂 was shot dead, 陈陈小娟 was raped unsuccessfully and then killed, and the houses were burned down. After the bandits were suppressed by the military, he fled to Shanghai. Due to the seriousness of the case, it was submitted to the Garrison Headquarters for review and then transferred to the District Court. The prosecutor completed the investigation and filed a public prosecution. Yesterday, Judge Deng opened the court hearing. Hu Xiaozhong testified that he was 32 years old, from Linyi, and lived in Shanghai's Sanguantang as a laborer. He claimed to have only worked as a laborer for a little over ten days before being arrested. Before that, he served in the Third Brigade in Qingdao under Brigade Commander Deng Haifeng, Regiment Commander Zhao Xuehong (later known as Zhao Fengmin), and Battalion Commander Wang Youxiang, who were stationed in Zhucheng. He then claimed to have been a fireman. He said he joined the army in 1926 and served for four years. He denied all charges of robbery, murder, and arson, claiming that Chen Qingtang and others were selling private salt, and he had previously intercepted their private salt shipments several times between 1925 and 1927 while working as a clerk in a salt shop in his hometown, and that they were now falsely accusing him out of spite. The judge noted that his statements were contradictory and his testimony was inconsistent. He ordered photographs to be taken for correspondence to the battalion to verify whether he had served in the military between 1926 and 1929 in order to reach a verdict. The plaintiff, Chen Qingtang, testified that he was 32 years old, from Nanquanzhuang, Linyi, and worked as a laborer in Shanghai. He said that he was not at home when the disaster struck his family, but his brother, Chen Chou, was a captive at the time. The judge then summoned Chen Chou, who testified that he was 19 years old and recognized the defendant. On the night of August 25, 1928, at 10:00 PM, Hu led over 500 bandits to attack their village, which lasted until 8:00 AM on the 26th. His parents and sister-in-law were all kidnapped. His brother was shot dead when he tried to escape, and his niece was beaten to death when she refused to become his wife. He later escaped, and his parents were redeemed for ten yuan. Another victim, Dong Shihe, testified that he was from Nanquanzhuang, Linyi, and the defendant's aunt was his sister-in-law. On August 25, Hu led bandits to attack the village and killed his three nephews, Gouer, Shun'er, and Deng'er. Liu Qingchi, Liu Qingtang, and others testified that their homes were burned down, but their family members were not harmed. The judge instructed that if there were more fellow villagers who were victims, they should come forward to testify so that the truth could be clarified. The plaintiffs claimed that there were many people from the same village in Shanghai who could all come. The judge instructed them to gather together and submit a written statement for summoning. The case was adjourned for further hearing, and the defendant was returned to custody.

Sheng Xuanhuai's Granddaughter Has Married

Another Lawsuit Over Division of Property

Wang Shengrong Sues Her Uncle Zechen

Demanding Division of Over 600,000

Lawsuits over the Sheng family's property in Biling have been occurring repeatedly. Now, Wang Shengrong, a granddaughter of Sheng Xuanhuai, has filed a lawsuit against her uncle, Sheng Zechen, and Zechen's son, Yuyou, also demanding a division of property. The late Aichen's two concubines, Gong and Zhang, have also been named as defendants. Sheng Zechen, Sheng Chongyi, Sheng Yuchang, and others have all come forward to participate as defendants, thus expanding the scope of the lawsuit. It is reported that Sheng Xuanhuai's first wife was Dong, and both Kui and Ai were born to Dong. The second wife was Zhuang. The plaintiff in this case, Rong, is the daughter of Kui and was adopted by Ai. Since Ai's children were all gone, Rong served Ai's two concubines, Gong and Zhang, with filial piety, and is naturally Ai's adopted daughter. Although Yuyou is the son of Zechen and has inherited Ai's lineage, Ai's estate, Madam Zhuang's private property, and the Yuzhai Charity Estate are all jointly owned by her and Yuyou, so she hired lawyer Li Zuyu to file a lawsuit against Ai's two concubines, Zechen, and his son, requesting a division of their assets totaling over 600,000. Zechen and Yuyou, who were sued, also hired lawyers Jiang Yiping and Jiang Baoli to defend themselves, claiming that the plaintiff was actually the daughter of the eldest son, Kui, and since Ai had no children, Yuyou, the son of the fourth son, Zechen, was adopted, which is completely legal. There is no such thing as establishing an adopted daughter in addition to an adopted son. The plaintiff's claim that Ai adopted the plaintiff in 1916 because he had no son is illogical. Even if she believes that she has the right to jointly divide 60% of the Yuzhai Charity Estate, the plaintiff can only claim that the property under the name of the eldest son, Kui, has no identity or name in the third room, so how can she fabricate facts to request a division? They requested that the original lawsuit be rejected. Yesterday morning, Judge Xu Wenyong opened the court. Both parties were represented by lawyers, and other participants also appointed lawyers to appear in court. After mutual arguments, the case was temporarily adjourned for review because the case was complex and required the plaintiff to provide a detailed statement of reasons.

A Licentious Son-in-Law

Seduces His Wife's Sister and Then Her Younger Sister

The Older Sister's Husband Becomes His Own Husband

Wang Nenghai, from Wusong, lives at No. 2 Baisazhong Road, in the French Concession. His daughter, Wang Shuzhen, is in her early twenties and has a beautiful appearance. She lost her mother at a young age and was raised by her father. She and her younger sister are unmarried. Recently, due to the opening of her romantic senses, she often visited her sister's husband, Chen Guitang, under the pretext of visiting her sister, and ended up developing a romantic relationship with Chen Guitang. Their love reached a boiling point. When her father, Wang Nenghai, found out, he took his daughter back and reprimanded her. However, Shuzhen actually ran away and started a new family with Chen Guitang, behaving like a married couple. After her father found out where she was, he reported it to the French police, who ordered an investigation and arrested Chen and Shuzhen together, taking them into custody. The couple tasted the flavor of a prison cell. Yesterday morning, they were sent to the French Court for questioning. First, the complainant, the girl's father, Wang Nenghai, stated that he lived on Youheng Road, Hongkou. His eldest daughter was seduced by the defendant, Chen Guitang, at the age of seventeen. Later, relatives mediated and formally married her to him as his wife. However, the complainant knew that his son-in-law was a licentious playboy and was afraid that he would seduce his second daughter, so he moved to a remote area at No. 2 Baisazhong Road, under his jurisdiction. Unexpectedly, Chen Guitang dared to take advantage of the complainant's absence on business trips to deceive and occupy his second daughter, Shuzhen. However, Chen's financial resources are limited and he is unable to take care of his wife, so how can he possibly support the younger sister? He requested that he be severely punished according to the law. As for the second daughter, Shuzhen, he requested that she be sent to the bureau because the complainant is away on business most of the time, and if he takes her back, she might be abducted again. Chen Guitang testified that he was a businessman in other cities. In August of last year, he left for business and returned to Shanghai in November. He learned that his wife was having an affair, so there were often disagreements in the family. His sister-in-law, Wang Shuzhen, often came to mediate, and day after day, the two of them went from friendship to love. When her father found out, he beat Shuzhen, so Shuzhen ran away and started a new family with him, which is true. Wang Shuzhen testified that last year, because her sister was having an affair, she had an argument with her brother-in-law. As a girl, she often went to mediate. Later, she saw that her brother-in-law treated her sister very well, so she developed a love for her brother-in-law. Now, she is willing to spend her life with her brother-in-law and does not want to go home. Although her father is her biological father, he often abused her, and she is afraid of him. Now that she is in her early twenties, according to the laws of the Republic of China, she should have the right to choose her own marriage. She requested that she be granted freedom and that the lawsuit be dismissed. Judge Zhu Chengshen consulted with the French Consul, Mr. Du, and ordered Chen to be released on bail and Wang Shuzhen to be detained while the police investigate whether Wang Shuzhen is over twenty years old and report back to the court for further questioning.

A Page of a Young Girl's Painful History

One Wrong Step Leads to Eternal Regret

Chen Yuemei, a woman of 24 years old from Guanyintang, Qingpu, lost both parents at a young age and was raised by her aunt, Li. Last autumn, she came to Xujiahui with a woman named Xu to learn lace making, and soon became a Catholic in the Catholic Church. In early February of this year, she was enticed by the rogue Yang Jinlong, and Yuemei was bewitched by him, so they formed a small family and lived together as a couple at No. 33 Qian Hu's House. In the beginning, they were still considered to be on good terms, but Yang associated with bandits and liked to gamble. He swindled all the lace wages obtained by Yuemei, and then pawned off her clothes and gold jewelry. Recently, he has ignored the family, and they are almost starving. When Yuemei asked him for money, she was beaten. Unexpectedly, Yang came the other day and claimed that if she wanted money, she could follow him. Yuemei had no choice but to follow Yang to the home of his mistress, Yang Shen, at No. 5 Xichengzhi Lane, Tangjie. He locked Yuemei in a room, surrounded her, and beat her until she was covered in injuries and her body was not intact. He also threatened to end her life with a pistol. Fortunately, a neighbor heard the noise and came to rescue her, so she was able to save her life. After Yuemei escaped, she went to the Sixth District, Second Branch of the Public Security Bureau in the town and requested an arrest. The police immediately dispatched officers to summon Yang Jinlong and Yang Shen to the station. After Chief Xu briefly interrogated them, Chen Yuemei testified that she had been enticed to a hotel by Yang Jinlong in February and was raped against her will under various threats. Her injustice was unpardonable for the rest of her life, and the defendant was a well-known local rogue with a large following, so she was afraid that her life would be difficult to protect in the future and that she could not face her parents in the afterlife. Therefore, she wished to break off all contact with him, ask for the return of the borrowed money, and go home to live. She pleaded to be tried for rape, and tears streamed down her face as she spoke. Yang Jinlong testified that he was 36 years old, from Kunshan, and worked as a telephone operator at the Nanyang University Telephone Office. He admitted to having an affair with Chen Yuemei and admitted to the beating. Chief Xu believed that the case involved enticement and rape and was inconvenient to handle, so he sent Chen Yuemei, Yang Jinlong, and Yang Shen to the District Court yesterday morning for strict handling according to the law.

Trial Record of a Madman Murder Case

Zhang Jiazhen Describes the Circumstances of the Murder

Zhang Jiazhen, a madman, killed a young woman, Wu Zhou, and a primary school student, Leng Cuibao, with a knife in front of the Qunxue Society at Xiaonanmen in March of this year. After being arrested by the patrol police, he was sent to a mental hospital. His mental state has gradually recovered, and the District Court has completed its investigation and filed a public prosecution. Yesterday, Judge Zhao opened the court hearing. Zhang Jiazhen testified that he was from Zhenjiang, and the knife was bought for ten cents by a Mr. Wang. He bought two knives, one for himself and one for Mr. Wang, who had already gone to Nanjing. He bought the knife not to kill people, but to sell beef. He didn't know what he was doing when he killed people. He hadn't bumped into the woman who was killed. Heaven told him to kill her. He had no grudges against the deceased. He wasn't lying. The child was watching him and was killed by him. There was also a child who hadn't died. He didn't know them either. Now he thinks about it, and he feels sad. He didn't kill the patrol police because he was going to shoot, so he scared him with a knife. He was willing to go to the police station and didn't want to escape. The judge asked, "Do you know that killing people is punishable by death?" He replied, "Heaven told me to kill them, so it's not my fault." The judge asked, "Are you willing to pay with your life?" Zhang couldn't answer. The judge asked, "Is there anyone who sold you out for pretending to be crazy and killing people?" He replied, "I want to pretend to be crazy. There is heaven and earth above and a beast below." The judge asked, "Why didn't you kill the other woman?" He replied, "She ran away." Witness He Jiumei testified that she was 21 years old, from Shanghai, and lived in Xiaonanmen. She and Wu Zhou were working in the factory. She saw Zhang Jiazhen grabbing Wu Zhou in Tianfuli. When she saw the knife, she immediately ran away, so she didn't know what happened after she was stabbed in the hand. The judge asked, "Did a young woman in your landlord Gong Xuexian's family ever have an argument with him?" She replied, "No." Leng Chuibao testified that he was 21 years old, from Zhenjiang, and lived at No. 44 Meijialong as a teacher. His brother, Cuibao, was killed by Zhang Jiazhen after leaving school and died in the hospital. He didn't witness it at the time. Fan Zhang testified that she was 37 years old, from Zhenjiang, and lived at Tashuiqiao. Her husband's name was Fan Zhusheng, and he sold newspapers. Zhang Jiazhen was her younger brother. He had come to her house twice this year and didn't call out to her. He just played with her two sons. She didn't invite him because there were many people in her house. He had been mentally ill when he was twelve or thirteen years old, but he recovered soon after. He hadn't been mentally ill for three years since coming to Shanghai, but his words were a little off. She didn't know he lived in Ma Tianxing Lane until the Third Branch of the First District told her after he killed someone. The judge believed that there were discrepancies in the sentencing of this case, so he ordered that the witnesses be subpoenaed again for verification. The defendant was returned to custody.

Recent News of the National Sugar Manufacturing Company

The National Sugar Manufacturing Company was operated by the Yizhong Banking Syndicate on behalf of the former National Sugar Factory in 1926 to compensate for outstanding debts. The planning and management were initially smooth, but the labor unrest and disputes caused by the political changes in the spring of 1927 were not resolved for a long time, resulting in huge losses and eventually leading to a shutdown. Last year, in order to protect the shareholders' capital and maintain the industry, the Ministry of Industry and Commerce sent personnel to organize a reorganization office to test-produce 10,000 tons of refined sugar in preparation for resuming operations. Now that the test production has been completed, the Ministry has ordered the reorganization office to return all the equipment to the Yizhong Banking Syndicate to facilitate the resumption of operations. It is reported that the Banking Syndicate has raised a large amount of capital and is making arrangements to proceed. Both parties have sent responsible personnel to the factory to carry out the handover since the day before yesterday. The Banking Syndicate has specially invited Lao Naixin to represent them in handling the takeover.

Origin of Stray Bullet in the Should-Be Office

A Mischievous Child Scared the Presiding Judge

According to the Shanghai Times, a hole was found yesterday (3rd) in the glass window of Judge Ying's office at the Special District Court. For a time, it was rumored that it was hit by a stray bullet. Later, after investigation by detectives, it was found that it was actually a mischievous child who used a toy gun to shoot a stone, accidentally hitting the glass window and causing the hole.

An Elderly Man Commits Suicide After Losing His Grandson

Hu Sanlin, a 61-year-old man from Gaoyou, used to pull a rickshaw. Recently, due to his old age, he shared a shift with another person (called a half-shift). His 60-year-old wife washed clothes for others, and his grandson, Heshang, 13 years old, rented a loft above the stove at No. 548 Fushou Lane, Jiaxing Road, Hongkou, to make a meager living. Heshang studied diligently and intelligently at a nearby private school. On the first day of this month, because of the abolished Lunar New Year Dragon Boat Festival holiday, Heshang went out to play after eating and did not return until late. The old couple searched everywhere in great anxiety. There was still no sign of him yesterday morning. Sanlin, feeling hopeless after his beloved grandson disappeared, suddenly embraced the idea of ending his life. He secretly swallowed opium to commit suicide in bed, sighing. His wife thought he was sleeping and didn't pay attention. When she called him for lunch and he didn't respond, she went to the bed and realized something was wrong. The landlord from Guangdong, Mr. Liang, heard the noise and came to see. He determined that he had taken poison and immediately sent him to the Gongji Hospital for treatment. According to the doctor, although the time of taking the poison was short, it was difficult to save his life due to his old age.

Important Meeting of the Opium Exchange Industry

Yesterday, the Shanghai Opium Exchange Industry Reorganization Committee held its sixth committee meeting at its office on Lloyd Road. Committee members Shen Qixiang, Qiu Tanglin, Chen Liangyu, Teng Zhixiang, Luo Yisheng, and others attended. First, the chairman reported on the progress of various reorganization matters. Then, the meeting resolved to proceed with election procedures as follows: (1) It was decided to convene a members' general meeting on June 20th at the Ningbo Association Hall, and an announcement would be published in newspapers for two days to inform the industry. (2) It was resolved that the membership applications submitted by industry members were now complete and that a membership list should be compiled according to the reorganization procedures and submitted to the Municipal Party Department and the Social Affairs Bureau for guidance and supervision of the election by representatives of the Reorganization Committee. (3) Upon receiving a letter from the Reorganization Committee setting a date for the Industry Representatives Conference and requesting the nomination of representatives to attend, it was resolved that the Reorganization Committee would nominate Committee Member Chen Liangyu as the association's representative. Membership dues would be paid according to regulations. (4) It was noted that the current price list for goods sold by industry members was insufficient due to rising living costs and increased costs, and that prices urgently needed to be adjusted to maintain capital. It was resolved to designate a special committee to assess sale prices in detail and publish them for all industry members to comply with. Any violations of the regulations would be subject to disciplinary action. This price list would be distributed twice a month. Any fluctuations within the period would be announced separately and at any time. (5) It was noted that the assistance fees allocated from the license tax on opium in the Second District to the northern and southern cities were long overdue. The association urgently needed to collect these funds to cover the costs of holding the elections. It was resolved to investigate the matter and send a formal letter of demand. (6) Committee Member Shen Qixiang proposed that the market expenses previously determined by the association should be collected from July 1st of this year, after the establishment of the general membership meeting, to maintain the association's affairs (Passed). (7) Committee Member Chen Liangyu proposed that all funds received by the association in the future should be deposited and withdrawn from designated banks at any time, and that three economic committee members should be designated to be responsible for safekeeping. Any withdrawals must be signed and sealed to show seriousness (Passed). Finally, committee members expressed their opinions in succession and the meeting adjourned.

Woman

Sues for Divorce Due to Husband's Abandonment

Fu Xia, a woman from Yancheng, has retained attorney Zhang Ding to file a lawsuit with the District Court, alleging that her husband, Fu Longchang, abandoned her and seeking a divorce. The petition states that she married the defendant in September of the thirteenth year of the Republic through a matchmaker. However, he indulged in debauchery and neglected his duties, disregarding their livelihood. She was forced to work in a factory as a female worker to make a living. The defendant not only failed to improve himself but squandered her wages. When he did not get his way, he would resort to physical violence. On October 31st of last year, while the plaintiff was at the factory, he took all her clothes and belongings and disappeared. After a long time, she inquired with his parents, but they ignored her. She advertised in the newspaper in January of this year, hoping for an early reunion, but he callously abandoned her and never returned home. Later, she learned that the defendant was at the Yong'an Company's Beijing opera theatre on April 6th, so she went to see him but was violently beaten and taken to the Nanjing Road police station. Because the case involved civil matters, she was instructed to file a lawsuit in court. The defendant has abandoned her for many years, and when she sought him out, she was beaten. The affection and righteousness between them are broken, and it is difficult to grow old together. Therefore, she requests permission to divorce. The defendant also submitted a defense, accusing the plaintiff of adultery with her maternal uncle, Zeng Changtai. Yesterday morning, Judge Tong Shengli specially opened the Fourth Court for trial. First, the plaintiff stated the previous situation. The court ordered Zeng Changtai to appear in court. He stated that he was 32 years old, from Yancheng, residing on Guoqing Road, and currently working at a certain amusement park. He was asked if he and Fu Xia were at Yong'an Company together. He replied that this was not the case and that he did not have time to play due to his work. He was asked if there was a Liu Xiaoxizi who seduced the plaintiff in the past, and if he negotiated at the scene afterward. He replied that he did. The court ordered the defendant, Fu Longchang, to appear in court. He testified that he pulls a cart for a living and does not want a divorce. Last year, on March 23rd, his wife was abducted by Liu Xiaoxizi, and he filed a lawsuit to bring his wife back. Unexpectedly, people told him that his maternal uncle, Zeng Changtai, was having an affair with his wife. He did not believe it until he returned home on September 27th of last year and caught them in the act. On the evening of April 6th this year, at 11:00 PM, someone informed him that his maternal uncle and his wife were playing at Yong'an Company, so he went there and grabbed his maternal uncle but was beaten and escaped. At that time, he took his wife to the police station and now asks the court for justice. The judge questioned Zeng Changtai again. He stated that these were all false accusations by Longchang, and that it was inappropriate for him, as an elder, to commit adultery with his nephew's wife. Because Longchang was usually unproductive, he would often educate him, which inevitably caused resentment. After that, he generally did not inquire about Longchang's family affairs. At this point, the plaintiff's lawyer stated that the defendant had accused the plaintiff and Zeng of adultery in the Procuratorate of this court, which was found not to be true. Furthermore, the plaintiff stated that the defendant was always unproductive, using lead coins and gambling, ruining her reputation, and shamelessly accusing her of adultery with her uncle. The neighbors are still there, and if there is any impropriety, they can be severely punished. The judge then invited Prosecutor Xu to appear in court and express his opinion. The plaintiff's lawyer then made a statement. The judge then announced that the debate was over and a verdict would be issued at 1:00 PM on the 7th of this month, and then adjourned the court.

Fiancé Wants Ten Times the Betrothal Gift

Ling Awu, a local woman residing at No. 38, Xiangyi Lane, Gonghexin Road, Zhabei, recently retained attorney Gong Yingxuan to sue her fiancé, Zhao Jiansheng, in the District Court, alleging that he has no legitimate occupation and that she did not consent to the engagement. The defendant replied that when the engagement was made, fifty yuan was given as a betrothal gift. If the plaintiff wants to terminate the engagement, she must pay ten times the penalty, five hundred yuan, before he will agree to terminate the engagement. The judge said, "How can that be? If you borrow money, the interest cannot exceed the principal. It is best to return the principal and interest. It is best to reconcile. There is no benefit in fighting a lawsuit. How much money will you spend after three trials? What benefits will you have?" The plaintiff interrupted and said, "There were only thirty-two yuan of betrothal gift when the engagement was made. Even if you double it, it is only sixty-four yuan." The matchmakers Ling Gengxin and Ling Yan also testified. The judge tried to reconcile them, but they did not agree, so he began the debate and considered it concluded, awaiting the verdict.

Looted Fishing Boat Redeemed After Payment

The Ningbo fishing boat "Jindeli," loaded with fresh yellow croaker for sale in Shanghai, arrived in Shanghai on the morning of the 19th of last month and berthed on the Pudong beach opposite the Jianghai Customs House in Wusong River, near the "Cedian" and "Junhe" warships. That night, it was stormed by Wen-Tai pirates who entered the port of Wusong and looted the fishing boat. The fish merchant Xie Alai confirmed the robbery and reported it to the Fourth District Water Police for pursuit, and requested the Jiangzhe Fisheries Association to send the "Fuhai" escort vessel to track and rescue it. Details were reported in the 23rd of last month. It is now learned that after the fishing boat was robbed, the pirates forced it to sail to Haimen, Taizhou, and communicated with the fish merchant Xie Alai, requesting him to prepare funds for ransom. After receiving the letter, the fish merchant immediately sent someone to negotiate with the pirates. It was agreed to redeem the boat for 800 yuan, and the payment has been completed. The fishing boat can now escape danger and will sail to Shanghai soon. However, according to the Zhejiang Public Association, the loss from the robbery to date is more than a thousand yuan.

Yesterday morning, the Wuxingji Sand and Stone Company of Wusong Wai Malu hired a Chongming Chen Yinji lighter to load forty tons of yellow sand to Paotaiwan. It encountered strong winds and waves, which caused the lighter and its cargo to sink. The five crew members fell into the water with the boat. Fortunately, it was daytime, and they were rescued by boatmen, so no one was injured. The customs and river police learned of the incident and tried to tow the lighter into the port, but the wind and waves were too strong, making it difficult to tow. They are now trying to find a way to tow and salvage it.

Milk Stall Owner

Acquitted After Appeal

Gu Jirong, the owner of the Johnson Milk Stall, was previously charged by the Public Works Department's Health Department with selling impure milk, endangering public health. Gu retained attorney Xi Yafu for his defense. The Primary Criminal Court of the Special District Court sentenced Gu Jirong to two months of imprisonment and a fine of 200 yuan. Gu appealed and retained attorney Chen Tingrui. The Criminal Court's Judge Xu Jiashi heard the case and publicly announced the verdict yesterday afternoon, reversing the original verdict and declaring Gu Jirong not guilty.

Deserter Jumps from Train and Dies

Yesterday, while a train on the Shanghai-Nanjing Railway was traveling from Changzhou to Shanghai, four soldiers who had overstayed their leave were being escorted by soldiers from Suzhou to Shanghai. At 4:50 PM, while the train was passing through Zhengyi Station, west of Kunshan Station, at a place called Shiwulian Dayang Bridge, one of the soldiers suddenly jumped out of the train door when the escorts were unprepared. He fell to the ground, cracking his head and splattering his brain matter. He died instantly. After the train arrived at Kunshan Station, the incident was reported to eastbound trains, and the dead soldier was taken to an empty lot at Zhengyi Station to await a report to the Three Provinces Bandit Suppression Headquarters for processing.

Be Careful When Russians Inquire

The North-China Daily News reported that recently, two well-dressed Russians have been frequenting foreign firms, shops, and offices. One asks questions as a pretext, while the other steals in the meantime. As the weather gets warmer, those wearing Western suits tend to remove their coats and hang them on hooks. These people take the opportunity to steal valuables from the coat pockets. On April 30th, No. 17 Museum Road, and yesterday (May 3rd), No. 21 Yuanmingyuan Road were successively robbed. In one case, one Russian pretended to inquire about the address of a certain foreign firm. The owner flipped through the directory for him, unaware that the wallet in his pocket had already been taken by the second Russian, resulting in a loss of 150 yuan. From now on, anyone who removes their coat should pay attention to these people.

Chen Xiting's Home Robbers Arrested

The Chauffeur Is Highly Suspected

Chen Xiting's home at 28 Lloyd Road was robbed by armed bandits on the afternoon of April 10th, who stole valuables worth a thousand yuan. The police have been investigating the case since the report was made, but there have been no clues. It was not until the other day that Detective Zhang Liang of the Laoza Police Station discovered that Chen Ge'er, a chauffeur from Haizhou who had previously worked for Chen's family, was highly suspected. Chen was arrested and confessed, and he also revealed that his accomplices Zhang Jingming and Zhang Deqiu were hiding at No. 340 Annan Near Road in the French Concession. The two Zhangs were also arrested yesterday and were sent to the Special District Court, where Judge Zhou interrogated them and ordered them to be detained for further questioning.

Xu Tianfu Acquitted

The Garrison Headquarters previously sent personnel to search for opium on a foreign ship in Hongkou. Wang Daxi, who was suspected of being the informant, was beaten by opium dealers. The police arrested Xu Tianfu and handed him over to the Special District Court, which sentenced him to eight months of imprisonment. Xu claimed that he was falsely accused by Wang and retained attorney Fan Gang to appeal for redress. The High Branch Court reviewed the case and announced the verdict yesterday afternoon, reversing the original verdict and finding Xu Tianfu not guilty.

Gambling Den Owner Zhu Ajin Fined 500 Yuan

Recently, the French police have been cracking down on flower club gambling very severely. The other day, Detective Xu Fuqing, Deputy Detective Tao Desheng, Li Yousheng, Li Liansheng, and Zou Rongsheng discovered that a rogue Zhu Ajin was running an illegal flower club at No. 109 Jincheng Lane, Grero Road, and had dispatched accomplices to set up listening posts and communication devices in the British, French, and Chinese territories to entice people to gamble, violating the prohibition. The detectives immediately reported to the Western Inspector and went together to arrest Zhu, seizing a flower club gambling kit: a large red brocade bag with embroidered flower patterns, containing a small card with the name of the flower club (Tianshen) and silver coins. Zhu was taken to the police station and then to the French Concession Court for investigation. The Western Inspector explained the situation. Zhu Ajin confessed to running an illegal flower club den. The Chinese and Western judges sentenced Zhu to a fine of 500 yuan, to be confiscated along with the seized items and silver coins.

Letter from China and Foreign Telephone Company to Shareholders

Letter from Shanghai China and Foreign Telephone Company Limited to shareholders: Esteemed Shareholders, The declaration issued on April 26th was not entirely clear. The directors can now inform the shareholders that the report of the advisory committee has been received. The report indicates that the directors share the same views regarding the company's adoption of an automatic telephone system (as detailed in the aforementioned declaration). As the directors fully agree with the advisory committee, they specifically recommend that the shareholders accept the tender from International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation so that the matters discussed in the report of the Public Works Department Commissioner can be implemented immediately and the highest quality automatic telephone service can be provided to the public in Shanghai without delay. For the complete understanding of all shareholders, the following documents are included in this booklet: (1) Report of the Advisory Committee, (2) Tender of International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation, (3) Tender of Ericson Telephone Company Limited, (4) Tender of Telegraph and Telephone Trust Limited. The decision to recommend accepting the tender of International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation is based on the fact that the directors have carefully considered this matter and have been advised by experts who have no interest in any particular system. As for the financial aspect, the directors believe that the price of 75 taels per share is quite fair, considering that the face value is only 50 taels and that the market price was only 65 taels and 5 qian at the time of the initial tender. The directors believe that the amount of profit that will be generated from the requested capital in the future is also reasonable, as it is still less than that of most other public utilities in Shanghai. Therefore, the directors hope that the shareholders will support their recommendation to sell the company's business to the new company organized by International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation. The report of the advisory committee and the tenders of the three companies have been submitted to the Shanghai Municipal Council and the French Municipal Council, requesting their approval to grant the patent to International Telephone and Telegraph Corporation. Once a written reply of approval is received, an extraordinary general meeting of shareholders will be convened. You will be notified of the date as soon as possible. With best wishes. Sincerely, Bell, Acting Chairman on behalf of the Board of Directors (May 28, 1930)

Letter

Dear Editor, The report in your newspaper's local news section about the Punam Group Police continuing to break up a bandit den not only contained inaccurate details, but also misrepresented the names of the people involved. I respectfully submit the true situation for publication in your newspaper to establish the facts. On May 7th, the kidnap victim Zhang Yuxing escaped from the bandit den and reported to Ye Yuyu and the Songjiang County Government. Upon receiving the report, Ye Yuyu, together with Deputy Township Head Ma Heshu, the local security officer Zhang Jingfang, and many villagers, raided the bandit den and captured the kidnappers Gu Guanlian (previously misidentified as Gu Liansheng) and Wang Jinyi, as well as the kidnap victim Zhang Zhujiang. The two bandits were sent to the Qiantang Harbor Ninth Precinct as an agent for the Nanhui County Government for legal action. The kidnap victim Zhang Zhujiang, due to his old age and prolonged confinement, requested to stay at the local security officer's home for one night. The next day, he filed a report with the county government. However, at 3:00 AM on the 8th, Zhang Yuxing, accompanied by Captain Shi of the Jiangsu Water Police, came with an official document from the Songjiang County Government to raid the bandit den. However, the bandits had already been transferred, and the kidnap victim had been rescued. Captain Shi took the kidnap victims Zhang Zhujiang and Zhang Yuxing to the Songjiang County Government for questioning and then released them. On the 10th, Inspector Shao Jingzhi of the Ninth Precinct, accompanied by Detective Yao, who was dispatched by Director Fang of the Nanhui County Public Security Bureau, hurriedly came to the township and insisted on taking the kidnap victim. We explained the situation in detail. They were furious and arrested Deputy Security Officer Luo Hongpu without raiding the bandit den. We had no choice but to go to Songjiang to ask the Songjiang County Government to return the kidnap victim Zhang Yuxing to Nanhui for filing a report and requesting the release of Hongpu. At this time, the County Public Security Bureau had no choice but to send the kidnappers to the County Government for legal action. However, Deputy Security Officer Luo Hongpu was still detained without release. After being imprisoned for four days, Zhang Yuxing was finally able to report to the Nanhui County Government, and Luo Hongpu was released after questioning. Currently, the kidnappers and kidnap victims have all been taken by Captain Shi to Songjiang for legal action. Ye Yuyu, Ma Heshu, Zhang Jingfang respectfully submit. Having read the news article "Prices of Livestock Intestines Continue to Rise" in the June 3rd issue of your newspaper, I am greatly astonished by the references to our factory. After investigation, our factory has not established branch factories in northern Anhui or southern Henan. The statement that "the stock in Shanghai is low, and there is no supply for the market" is contrary to the facts. Therefore, I request that you make a correction to avoid confusing the market. Sincerely, Guo Shunji
